Director of the Jiande Bank

This is Not Ma Yun-chu, But Ma Yin-chu

Ma Yin-chu Will Issue a Statement

Recently, various newspapers in Shanghai carried the news of the closure of Jiande Bank. One section mentioned that Ma Yin-chu was a director of the bank. A reporter specifically visited Mr. Ma at Jiaotong University to inquire about the matter. Mr. Ma stated that last year, the bank sent his secretary, a Mr. Zheng, to Hangzhou to invite him to serve as chairman of the board of directors. He firmly declined because he was not familiar with the bank's internal affairs and was not a shareholder. He then received a letter from the bank saying that he had already been elected as chairman of the board. He replied with a letter stating that he would not accept the position and that it was not legal according to the company law. Later, he received another letter from the bank saying that a board meeting would be held on a certain day and asking him to go to Shanghai to attend and assist the patriots' association.

Petition Representatives Returned to Shanghai Yesterday

Satisfactory Result, Granted Amnesty

Legislative Reduction of Rent Ordered for Handling

The Shanghai All Circles' Association for Aiding Patriotic Martyrs and the Committee for Reducing Rent, in order to request the Central Government to issue a clear order to pardon patriotic martyrs Liu Chongwu and others, and to promulgate rent reduction regulations, respectively dispatched representatives to Beijing on the seventh of this month to petition. They have obtained considerable results and returned to Beijing by train yesterday. The details of the petition process are recorded below:

Petition Representatives Returned to Shanghai Yesterday

The All Circles' Association for Aiding Patriotic Martyrs, on the grounds that patriotic martyrs Liu Chongwu, Zeng Songtao, Tian Shuiyang, and Pan Hongsheng, in the winter of the 21st year [of the Republic, i.e., 1932], were arrested by the Public Concession Police for throwing bombs to warn treacherous merchants, and were transferred to the First Special District Court and sentenced to severe penalties. Various legal groups in the city have repeatedly appealed for amnesty, but have not been granted approval. Recently, Pan Hongsheng accumulated resentment and became ill, and was on his deathbed. Fearing that Liu Chongwu and others might follow Pan's fate, representatives of various groups, including Hu Fengxiang, Chen Jiufeng, Yu Yaoqiu, Wang Jingdong, and Chen Peide, were elected as representatives and went to Beijing by express train on the seventh of this month to petition the Fifth Plenary Session, the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Judicial Yuan, and other agencies, requesting amnesty for them. They have achieved considerable results and returned to Shanghai by train yesterday afternoon.

Central Government Sympathetic and Grants Amnesty

Petition representatives Hu Fengxiang, Chen Jiufeng, Yu Yaoqiu, Wang Jingdong, and Chen Peide arrived in Beijing on the morning of the eighth. After resting briefly at the Central Hotel, they went to the Central Party Headquarters to petition. They were received by Secretary Ye Shizhi, who promised to submit the letter to the Secretary-General of the Fifth Plenary Session for review. They then went to the National Government, where they were received by Chief Secretary Wei Huai, who said that he would forward it to Chairman Lin and order the relevant authorities to handle it. Finally, they went to the Judicial Yuan, where they were received by Secretary-General Chen Gemei, who also gave a very satisfactory reply. At that time, the representatives believed that this trip was of great importance, and they could not return to Shanghai to report until they had personally met with the responsible officials. Representative Hu Fengxiang returned to Shanghai that evening because he felt slightly unwell. Chen, Yu, and Wang remained in Beijing to appeal. On the morning of the ninth, they went to the Judicial Yuan again and were personally received by President Ju. The representatives presented the earnest wishes of the various groups in person. Mr. Ju replied that he would be responsible for providing relief. The representatives were satisfied and left. In the afternoon, they visited various central committee members in Beijing to request justice in the General Assembly. The results were also very satisfactory. On the morning of the tenth, they went to the Fifth Plenary Session to petition and were received by Secretary-General Ye Chucang, who said that he would submit the presentation to the General Assembly and instruct the relevant authorities to handle it and asked the representatives to return to Shanghai that day and wait for the results. Therefore, the result has achieved a considerable purpose. They took the early express train back to Shanghai yesterday (the eleventh) to report the process to the Aid Association.

Regularly Scheduled Meeting to Report the Process

The All Circles' Association for Aiding Patriotic Martyrs, because this time the representatives were dispatched to Beijing to petition, requesting amnesty for Liu Chongwu and others, the result was quite satisfactory. In order to report the process to the various groups, it is now scheduled to convene a temporary executive committee meeting at 2:00 p.m. on the sixteenth of this month (Saturday) at the Tianhougong Bridge Meeting Hall, and to dispatch representatives to visit the families of the problem fighters and comfort the fighters in prison.

Petition to Reduce Rent Ordered for Review and Handling

In the future, the educational funds of various provinces can be uniformly allocated from the salt tax to consolidate the foundation of education and establish a century-long plan. I respectfully offer my humble opinions and ask for your consideration. In my urgent telegram, I cannot help but await your command."

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Telegraphed to Advise and Warn Stamp Inspectors

Do not act hastily

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday telegraphed to the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, saying, "The letter from the Biscuit Candy Canned Food Industry Association received on the eighth of this month stated, 'Our association has received a letter from member Taikang Company, reporting that a stamp tax bureau inspector recently came to our company to inspect stamps with a detective from the police. They shouted and rushed around, and the situation was tense, as if they were arresting important criminals. As a result, 27 account books were taken away, 23 of which were copies of the daily business volume reports from each branch to the head office. The original books with sufficient stamps affixed are kept in each branch. These copies are sent to the head office for reference on a daily basis, and there is no need to affix stamps again. This can be based on the tax bureau's reply letter explaining,' etc. Accordingly, it is found that the inspectors inspect the stamps, and if there are any omissions, the maximum punishment is to be imposed in accordance with the regulations. It cannot be equated with illegal or criminal behavior that violates the law. Inspectors should act peacefully and guide in a gentle and tactful manner when performing their duties. How can they act like a bully, arrogant and unreasonable? This matter is related to disturbing the peace of the shops, and it is necessary to transfer the letter to the tax bureau for strict correction. Moreover, there is an explanation that copies do not need to be stamped. Please also ask your association to negotiate with the tax bureau and present it to the Ministry of Finance for thorough investigation and prevention, so as to reassure the business community," etc. When the association arrived, it was found that when the stamp tax was executed, the person concerned should be treated with a peaceful attitude, explaining the reasons and ordering him to hand over the documents that should be stamped. Do not act hastily. Not only have the orders and advice of the Ministry of Finance been historically obeyed, but also this article is included in Article 13 of the recent Inspection Rules for Stamp Tax. Public officials who execute inspections in various places should abide by them uniformly. However, the Shanghai Special Zone has historically had a cooperative relationship with detectives. These people have accumulated habits under foreigners and rely on the fact that laws and judgments are beyond their reach. All measures are enough to make merchants pay attention. Moreover, with the relationship between commission and reward, it is inevitable to act hastily. The company that feels this kind of pain is not only Taikang Company. Now that the Ministry of Finance has promulgated the Inspection Rules for Stamp Tax, the Shanghai Special Zone should also have the obligation to respect and abide by it. In view of the previous situation, it is appropriate to prepare another document and telegraph to the Ministry of Finance for review, and to order the competent authorities to advise and warn strictly, so as to make public use. Keng, Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce."

Reduction in Water Depth in the Port Channel on the East Coast

Ships should pay attention when passing through

The Hydrographic Office issued a notice regarding the reduction in water depth in the Niupishan Port Channel near Xiangshanpu on the east coast. The reduced azimuth is calculated as (A) due north 64 degrees, distance 3.4 chains (B) due north 3.17 degrees distance 4 chains, from the top of the 400-foot mountain of Niupishan (every ten minutes is equivalent to one nautical mile, that is, east longitude about 122 degrees 2 minutes, north latitude about 29 degrees 39 minutes. The above two azimuths have a water depth reduction of one to two fathoms. Ships should pay attention when passing through.

Petition for the Families of the Victims of the Taishan Ship

The Taishan ship of the Sanbei Company has been in distress for nearly two weeks. According to the association's information, it sent a letter to the Sanbei Company saying, "After the Taishan ship disaster, the matter of searching for corpses, placing them in coffins, and providing generous condolences and handling the aftermath has been communicated to your company on the fourth of this month. However, several days have passed and there has been no reply. Now, according to the notification from the families of the victims, the company is currently only willing to pay the arrears of the crew's salary. Other condolences are temporarily not discussed and are considered inappropriate and unwilling to accept. Given the scale of your company and the virtue and prestige of the person in charge, you are always enthusiastic about supporting social welfare, so why would you be harsh to others when things happen to you and endure sitting by and watching the families of the victims wait to die? It is appropriate to send a letter accordingly, asking you to investigate and reply."

Petition to the Government from the Five Exchange Brokers' Associations

Requesting a Temporary Suspension of Exchange Tax Collection

A joint petition from the brokers' associations of the Flour, Cotton Yarn, Securities, Gold, and Miscellaneous Grains Exchanges to the Legislative Yuan and the Ministry of Finance, requesting a temporary suspension of the exchange tax collection, states: "In recent years, the world has been plagued by the economic crisis, and domestically, we have been beset by the concurrent pressures of floods, droughts, and banditry, leading to increasing rural bankruptcy and famine. Commerce and industry are in decline, and the circulation of wealth is increasingly constricted. China's overall economic activity is deteriorating, and the prospect of a crisis fills us with dread. The exchange is the command center of modern economic organization. Since the economy is in such a state of decline, its manifestation in the exchange is the gradual decline of buying and selling. Taking the trading volume of flour as an example, in 1931, it still reached around 30,000 bags; in 1932, it had decreased to 10,000 bags; and in 1933, it was less than 10,000 bags. In three years, it has gradually decreased by two-thirds. As for the gold industry, this year's trading volume is only half of that in 1930. The buying and selling of other items, such as securities, cotton yarn, and miscellaneous grains, are all in the same situation, trending towards decline. The business of merchants depends entirely on the amount of buying and selling transactions. Therefore, the large reduction in trading volume indirectly indicates the decline in the business of merchants. Furthermore, for several years, although business conditions have reached a dead end, merchants have still maintained this depressed situation, always with the aim of revitalizing commerce and industry. The exchange is the price stabilization mechanism for commerce and industry, the centralized mechanism for large-scale supply and demand in commerce and industry, the adjustment mechanism for supply and demand in commerce and industry, the risk transfer mechanism for commerce and industry, and the commodity circulation mechanism for commerce and industry. Therefore, if merchants only consider their own interests and fail to maintain this bleak situation, it would be tantamount to inflicting a fatal blow to China's entire commerce and industry, making the dim future of commerce and industry even darker. The stagnation of the exchange would also create opportunities for foreigners to control our commerce and industry. In the past, before Chinese-owned exchanges were established, the market prices of all commodities were based on the prices of foreign-owned trading houses and Japanese-owned exchanges. All price fluctuations were based on the interests of foreigners, while Chinese people were in a passive position, allowing foreigners to control China's economic power. Therefore, learning from the past, merchants, despite their declining profits, are unwilling to easily abandon the Chinese-owned exchanges that have been gained over the past decade, and give foreigners the tools to subvert and manipulate our commerce and industry. In recent years, merchants have provided considerable convenience to those who entrust buying and selling transactions in the exchange, to the extent possible, such as reducing commissions and providing advances on trading margins. As long as it is within their capabilities, they will do everything possible to accommodate them. More convenience for buyers and sellers means more opportunities for activity in China's commerce and industry. As for government bond trading, more convenience for buyers and sellers means not only more opportunities for activity in the commercial, industrial, and financial sectors, but also more flexibility in the management of national finances. However, reducing commissions and advancing margins are not only sacrifices and losses for the personal interests of merchants, but also involve great risks. Therefore, in recent years, the business of merchants has not only declined on the surface, but has also been a sacrifice in reality. Our government authorities are well aware of this situation and do not need merchants to complain about it. Recently, we heard that the Ministry of Finance intends to levy a considerable transaction tax on buying and selling in the exchange, and the tax rate has been submitted to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation. In theory, merchants would not dare to oppose the collection of this transaction tax. However, in light of today's reality, in order to save the depressed commercial situation, it is necessary to temporarily suspend the collection of the transaction tax. Otherwise, the tax rate must be suitable for China's current situation and should be reduced to a level that buyers and sellers can bear. The organization and legislation of our country's exchanges are mostly based on Japan. Now, let us cite the Japanese transaction tax rate for reference:

Japanese Exchange Tax Law (Revised in April, 1922), Article 5: "For buying and selling transactions within the exchange that are settled by the transfer of margin differences, a transaction tax shall be levied on the amount of each transaction agreement at the following tax rates: Category 1: Buying and selling transactions of local bonds or corporate bonds: A. Transactions with a performance period within seven days: 0.006%. B. Other: 0.01%. Category 2: Buying and selling transactions of securities: A. Transactions with a performance period within seven days: 0.015%. B. Other: 0.025%. Category 3: Buying and selling transactions of commodities: 0.025%. The tax shall not be waived even if the buying and selling contract is canceled. Article 7: Buying and selling transactions of national bonds shall not be subject to transaction tax."

From the intent of the Japanese Exchange Tax Law, the following points can be summarized: 1. No tax is levied on spot transactions, and the transaction tax is limited to futures trading (forward or periodic). Spot trading within the exchange is no different from spot trading outside the exchange. If no tax is levied outside the exchange, why should it be different inside the exchange? The reason for taxing futures trading is to make the exchange market more robust. 2. For periodic trading of securities, the tax is lower for short-term and higher for long-term, reflecting the nature of securities trading and the desire to shift from a long-term to a short-term basis. 3. The commodity transaction tax is the same as the long-term transaction rate for securities, because short-term transactions in the commodity futures market are not of great significance in the exchange, so there is no need to reduce the tax rate to encourage them. 4. National bond transactions are not taxed, in order to promote the popularity and flexible circulation of national bonds. In essence, there is no need to impose a high tax rate to suppress speculation. 5. Buying and selling transactions of local bonds and corporate bonds have a lower tax rate than other types of transaction taxes, in order to promote their popularity and flexibility. 6. The transaction tax is levied on the agreed amount, so when settlement and offsetting are carried out according to the opposite transaction, both the previous and subsequent agreements are taxed. When actual delivery is carried out, only half of the offsetting transaction is taxed. Swap transactions are not taxed separately because they are not new transactions.

Looking back at the current situation in our country, the level of economic development is far inferior to Japan, the foundation of the exchange is not as solid as Japan's, and the overall economic situation is not as good as Japan's. Therefore, if our country must collect a transaction tax today, there are many aspects of Japan's current tax law that can be adopted. What needs to be noted is that, given the current depression of commerce and industry in our country, the collection of the tax should be temporarily suspended or the tax rate should be reduced as much as possible. In other words, in the current economic downturn in our country, the following four points must be the principles for collecting transaction tax: 1. Buying and selling of national bonds and local public bonds should be exempt from tax. 2. For periodic trading of securities (including stocks, corporate bonds, and others), the tax should be lower for short-term and higher for long-term. The tax rate for the former should not exceed 0.0025%, and the tax rate for the latter should not exceed 0.005%. 3. The tax rate for commodity trading should not exceed 0.005%, regardless of whether it is short-term or long-term. 4. Commodity trading should be taxed based on the agreed amount of the transaction, not based on the quantity.

In conclusion, in today's China, where economic crises are breaking out on all sides, the entire nation must cultivate its vitality and strive to recover in the short term. Excessive transaction tax collection may cause unexpected economic panic. Merchants have been making their greatest efforts to contribute to the future development of China's commerce and industry, so we dare to present our humble views for consideration."

Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau

Preparing to Inspect Imported Livestock

Starting with Dairy Cows?

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry has only inspected exported livestock products, not imported livestock. It is heard that the Ministry of Industry believes that in recent years, unprecedented diseases in our country's livestock have mostly been introduced from abroad and spread inland, causing great harm. For example, contagious bovine pleuropneumonia and abortion disease have gradually spread throughout the country due to the lack of inspection of imported foreign livestock, resulting in great losses. In order to prevent the introduction and spread of such livestock diseases, it is necessary to start inspecting imported livestock as soon as possible. It is reported that the project will start with imported dairy cows from Shanghai and then gradually extend to other livestock. The Bureau has received an order from the Ministry of Industry to prepare for the project and has submitted detailed rules and estimates to the Ministry for approval. It is currently engaged in preparations and it is expected that inspection can be implemented by January of next year.

Jianghai Customs' Subsidy Measures for Exported Firewood Tax

Tax Rate Calculated at One Dime Per 100 Kilograms

The Jianghai Customs has issued a notice regarding the temporary subsidy measures for the tax on firewood transported abroad, in accordance with the order. The notice is as follows: "In accordance with the order of the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance, all exported firewood shall be taxed according to the tariff on a per-quantity basis. If it exceeds 5% of the value, it shall be taxed at 5% of the value based on the original percentage of the quantity tax, as a temporary subsidy measure. We shall comply with this order. From December 1st of this year, all firewood transported abroad shall be calculated at a rate of one dime (National Currency) per 100 kilograms according to Tariff No. 152 of the Export Tariff. If the tax collected exceeds 5% of the value, it shall be temporarily taxed at 5% of the value. However, firewood transported within the country to various ports shall still be taxed at the corresponding tax rate in the Transit Tariff. All merchants are hereby informed. Superintendent Tang Hai'an. Customs Commissioner Botlerd."

Xin Pinghu Steamer Aground in Fog

Xin Sheng News Agency reports: The Pinghu-Shanghai Steamer Bureau has three steamers: Xin Pinghu, Shanghai, and Lao Pinghu, which run exclusively between Shanghai and Pinghu. Now Lao Pinghu has been leased out. Xin Pinghu and Shanghai steamers are dispatched daily at 7:00 AM and 1:00 PM, departing from Pinghu and Shanghai respectively, carrying passengers and cargo. The Xin Pinghu steamer departed from Pinghu for Shanghai on the morning of the 10th of this month. At around 7:00 AM, when it arrived at Lugong Bridge, it ran aground due to heavy fog.

Relay Arrives in Shanghai: After the Xin Pinghu steamer ran aground, the captain discovered that the stern propeller had been damaged, resulting in the loss of steering capability. Therefore, all the cargo and passengers were transferred to the shore. At 1:00 PM, the company's Shanghai steamer departed from Pinghu. When it passed the location, it transferred the cargo and passengers to Shanghai. After arriving in Shanghai at 5:00 PM, the incident was reported to the Shanghai company.

Borrowed Steamer Maintains Service: The company considered that the suspension of steamer service was a major issue for transportation. Therefore, it borrowed the Xin Min Sheng steamer from the Minnan Steamer Company and it departed from Shanghai as usual at 1:00 PM on the 10th. At the same time, the Shanghai steamer was dispatched from Shanghai to Pinghu at 7:00 AM on the 11th. After arriving, efforts would be made to tow the Xin Pinghu steamer to Shanghai for repairs in the shipyard. The company also borrowed the Lao Min Sheng steamer from the Minnan Steamer Company and it departed from Shanghai for Pinghu at 1:00 PM on the 11th. However, the 1:00 PM sailing from Pinghu to Shanghai had to be temporarily suspended.

Shensha Steamer Cooperation Dissolves After Yongjia Steamer Joins

Fierce Price Competition Between Companies

Xin Sheng News Agency reports that after the Shensha steamer companies formed a cooperative office, it has now been decided to dissolve the office due to the addition of the Yongjia steamer, represented by the Sanbei Company. Details are as follows:

After Cooperation

The steamer companies operating between Shanghai and Qiming, Haimen, and Qidong, such as the Ping An Company's Baohua, the Dada Company's Guangxiang, the Daxing Company's Daxing, the Yuxing Company's Xin Renhe, and the Jufeng Company's Baofeng, totaling five ships, established the Shensha Steamer Cooperation Office on June 12th of this year, implementing cooperation and unifying water freight and passenger tickets to avoid competition, with excellent results.

Contract Dissolved

The Sanbei Steamer Company converted the former Dachang steamer to the Yongjia steamer and, represented by the company, joined the Shensha route and began operating on the 6th of this month. As a result, the Shensha steamer companies decided to dissolve the Shensha Steamer Cooperation Office after a meeting, and signed a dissolution agreement on the 8th of this month, which took effect on the 9th, with the office closed and the organization dissolved, returning to the individual companies for management.

Price War

On the day of the dissolution, the steamer companies immediately engaged in price competition, such as: (1) Passenger tickets: during cooperation, first-class cabins were $1.80, now $1.00; second-class cabins were $1.20, now $0.80; third-class cabins were $0.80, now $0.60; and steerage was $0.60, now $0.40. (2) Water freight: during cooperation, import and export goods were charged at 80% of the tariff rate; now it has been halved. The main import goods are soybeans and wheat, and the main export goods are groceries and sugar. It is expected that the above prices will continue to fall.

Performing at the Great Stage to Raise Relief Funds

The Shanghai Fundraising Committee for Drought Relief in Various Provinces, led by fundraising director Du Yuesheng, committee members Zhang Weiru, and Kui Yanfang, launched a theatrical performance to raise funds, scheduled for the evenings of the 13th, 14th, and 15th of this month at the Great Stage on Second Avenue. Famous sea opera amateurs are invited to participate in the performance. However, Mr. Mei has promised to perform on stage at a later date after returning to Shanghai to help the victims.

Coppersmith Robbed, Bound, and Imprisoned

Injured Falling From Window

Shuisheng You, a native of Ningbo, is 30 years old. He lives at No. 8, Taipingfang, Yucai Road, Hongzhen. He is a coppersmith at Yuanchang Machinery Factory on Yuezhou Road. At 2:00 PM yesterday, when Shuisheng You was repairing machinery at a tobacco factory at No. 3 Depei Lane, Yokohama Road, Zhabei, two robbers suddenly appeared, holding guns. The robbers mistakenly thought Shuisheng You was the owner of the factory and tied his hands with ropes. Being upstairs, the robbers began searching. They took dozens of silver dollars and a gold ring. While the robbery was taking place, Shuisheng You took the opportunity to escape from the window, intending to blow a police whistle to alert others. In a hurry, Shuisheng You mistakenly stepped on the lead-glass skylight and fell, injuring his left shoulder and hip. Someone called the police at post No. 2525 of the North Station Branch, who rushed to the scene and hired a rickshaw to send him to Renji Hospital for treatment.

(Shen Bao Third Sheet)

South District Rent Reduction Committee

Sends Representatives to Beijing to Petition

Suggesting the Fifth Plenary Session

The Shanghai Nanshi District Rent Reduction Committee held a meeting yesterday at the committee's hall in Yongqing Lane, Minkuo Road. The meeting was chaired by Wei Chaopin, recorded by Shen Qingzhai, and the following resolutions were passed: (1) Mr. Shi Liangcai, the General Manager of Shen Bao, was a pioneer in the press. His tragic assassination is deeply mourned. This committee should send Shen Qingzhai, Wu Benshan, Shan Fei, and Zhou Rulin to attend the memorial service. Resolution: passed. (2) Shao Tinglu, the director of the accounting department of this committee, dismissed staff member Wu Benshan without cause. This is an abuse of power. How should this be handled? Request a public decision. Resolution: Based on the public vote, Shao Tinglu, the director of the accounting department, was dismissed. (3) The Fifth Plenary Session has opened. Should this committee send representatives to Beijing to petition? Resolution: Send Shen Xinfu, Ni Yiwan, Wei Chaopin, Sun Nai, Wu Zaitang, etc. to Beijing to petition. The meeting adjourned. The petition is recorded below and presented to the meeting for discussion and a decision. A letter is to be sent to the National Government, ordering the Shanghai Municipal Government, the local court, and all agencies to assist the associations in implementing rent reduction to save the people's lives. The reasons are as follows: It is estimated that Shanghai has a population of 5 million. Except for landowners, property owners, and foreigners, who number about 500,000, the remaining 4.5 million people must rent houses. The rent paid each year, on average, accounts for about two-thirds of their annual income. In the past, when the market was prosperous and commerce was thriving, they could barely manage and were not completely destitute. Now, with the global economic crisis and the surge of rural bankruptcy in China, the impact on Shanghai is obvious and undeniable. If this continues, not only will commerce be unable to prosper and the market will be unable to thrive, but also this huge population will starve to death and will not be able to survive. This is the first reason why rent reduction should be vigorously implemented. Since the January 28th Incident in Shanghai, vitality has been almost lost and not yet recovered. Poverty is increasing, and beggars and starving people fill the streets. People are too busy saving their lives to have any purchasing power. Therefore, goods are piling up and sales are difficult, finance is stagnating, and the imbalance is alarming. Various tragic realities are presented before our eyes. The reasons are complex, but the biggest reason is that rents are too high. The blood and sweat of most citizens, in addition to paying most of their money for rent, are not enough to keep them warm and fed. This is the second reason why rent reduction should be vigorously implemented. Since this committee was established in January of this year, it has been working actively, day and night. Now, in Shanghai, under organized control, the establishment of branch committees and sub-committees in various lanes and neighborhoods, calling for action, has spread throughout the city. As a result, rent reductions have been achieved, such as in the Minkuo Road area, where it has reached one-third. However, many greedy and stubborn people, using the law as protection, relying on the concession as a stronghold, either ignore the call or file lawsuits, while many remain on the sidelines. Although we have repeatedly petitioned the party and government agencies, this matter is important. Without the power of political forces, it is not enough to raise awareness. This is the third reason why we should request the meeting to discuss the matter and make a decision, and send a letter to the administrative agencies to assist us. The methods are as follows: (1) The meeting should discuss the matter in detail, make a decision, and send a letter to the National Government, ordering the Shanghai Municipal Government, the local court, and all agencies to provide assistance in various ways, so that this rent reduction movement can be deepened and spread widely, in order to achieve complete success. (2) According to the Shanghai land price standards promulgated by the Shanghai Land Bureau this year, calculate the land price and add the construction cost to determine the cost of the house. The rent rate should be determined according to this cost. In addition to the landlord's land tax and house tax, it should not exceed the statutory amount (originally 10%, but now it is too high, and it is specified separately by the court). For those whose construction date is unknown, an estimate must also be made, so that fairness and impartiality are the criterion and both the landlord and tenant can be at peace. Rent reduction is a need of the times, and we speak out on behalf of the people. We ask the officials of the party and the state to pay attention to the suffering of the people and to discuss and approve this proposal in the meeting for discussing national affairs, and to implement it vigorously, then Shanghai will be fortunate and China will be very fortunate. This matter concerns the lives of the people, and we anxiously await rescue. Respectfully presented to the Presidium of the Fifth Plenary Committee of the Central Committee.

Heavy Fog in Wusong Estuary

Another Report on Capsized Sailboat

Hua'an Shipowner Claims Sailboat Self-Collided

Six People Rescued by Hua'an on the Spot

The Dang'an Company sent a letter to this newspaper yesterday, stating: "To the Editor: We have just seen a report in today's newspaper about the Hua'an steamer sinking a large sailboat in the heavy fog, which is slightly inconsistent with the facts. The Hua'an steamer arrived at this port last night. According to the captain's report, at 1:00 PM today (the 10th), it anchored near the S.E. Knoll buoy due to the fog. At 1:40 PM, a sailboat, fully rigged and moving with the current, sailed towards the bow of the Hua'an. Seeing this situation, the ship immediately ordered the sailors to loosen the anchor chain to reduce the force of the sailboat's collision. However, time was pressing, and it was too late. The hull of the sailboat was damaged, and seawater poured in. The captain of the sailboat, seeing the dangerous situation, wanted to turn the rudder to approach the Hua'an in order to escape. However, the tidal currents were turbulent, and there was a second collision, damaging the ship".

Urgent Relief Universal Donation from Wealthy Individuals Begins Immediately

Children's Army Donation Not Yet Fully Completed

Worker Donation Still in Progress

Central News Agency reports: Since the establishment of the Urgent Disaster Relief Universal Donation Committee, the General Affairs Department has been extremely busy. For days, they have been handling the clearing, registration, and completion of the Children's Army Universal Donation. The procedures have been cumbersome. Up until the night before last, the universal donations submitted to the committee totaled over 9,000 yuan. According to the council, because not all groups have submitted their donations, the total amount cannot be finalized until one or two more days.

Yesterday, schools came to the committee to submit donations and receipts, including: Junpu Elementary School, 7 silver dollars, 80 silver dimes, and 19,000 copper coins; Ningbo School, 55 silver dollars and 5 dimes; Jing'an Elementary School, 22 silver dollars and 586 silver dimes; Shibei Elementary School, 26 silver dollars, 160 silver dimes, and 25,300 copper coins; Minli Elementary School, 3 silver dollars, 116 silver dimes, and 1,910 copper coins; Dongming Elementary School, 11 silver dollars and 288 silver dimes; Wanzhu Elementary School, 280 silver dollars and 8 dimes, and 7 copper coins; Zhenxin Elementary School, 10 silver dollars and 291 silver dimes; Zhongdao Elementary School, 10 silver dollars and 258 silver dimes; Huaien Elementary School, 15 silver dollars and 380 silver dimes; Gaoqiao Elementary School, 19 silver dollars, 10 silver dimes, and 20 copper coins; Suzhou Students in Shanghai Elementary School, 21 silver dollars and 7 silver dimes; Yucai Elementary School, 41 silver dollars and 5 silver dimes; Huiqun Girls' High School, 52 silver dollars and 791 silver dimes; Xiude Elementary School, 65 silver dollars; Zhenxi Elementary School, 4 silver dollars and 304 silver dimes; Qingnian Middle School, 30 silver dollars and 1,000 silver dimes; Mingcheng Elementary School, 9 silver dollars and 4 dimes, and 378 silver dimes; Bide Elementary School, 80 silver dollars and 648 silver dimes; Minghui Elementary School, 38 silver dimes; Qizhi Elementary School, 10 silver dollars and 200 silver dimes. In addition, from private individuals: Mr. Chen Xihua donated 28 silver dimes, and Mr. Kuming donated 2 silver dollars.

Over ten schools, including Qiuzhi, Qianjiang, Zhennan, Liuyun, Aiqun, Weixing, and Mingde, sent letters to the committee to collect receipts. Over 200 elementary, middle, and high schools have not yet come to the committee to collect their receipts. The committee has sent letters urging them to come within three days to collect their receipts. Those who fail to collect their receipts by the deadline will be publicly announced in the news. As for the worker universal donation, in addition to the municipal government issuing notices and publishing announcements in the newspaper for all workers, staff, and factories to deduct and submit donations to the Shanghai Bank, the General Labor Union has also, in conjunction with various labor unions, notified all workers in the city. The Urgent Disaster Relief Universal Donation Committee has also sent letters to all factories, starting immediately, to handle the universal donations of factory workers and staff, and to quickly remit the donations to the Shanghai Bank to help the disaster victims.

The donation from wealthy individuals is the most important donation for the universal relief effort. In addition to the Universal Donation Committee conducting its own thorough investigation into the names, aliases, addresses, and occupations of wealthy individuals residing in Shanghai, it has also sent letters to the drought relief associations in various provinces for further investigation. This is expected to be completed in the next few days. After a meeting is held in the coming days, the universal donation from wealthy individuals will begin.

The Urgent Relief Committee recently sent letters to the Railway Bureau, Telephone Bureau, Post Office, and Jiangnan Shipyard, requesting them to encourage all staff and workers to donate to the urgent relief effort for the disaster areas, so as to accumulate small contributions into a large sum and provide universal relief to the disaster victims. Yesterday, Ni Tianyu from the Jiangnan Shipyard came to the committee to discuss the matter and collect the receipt procedures. It has been decided that starting today, donations will be solicited from all employees.

Among the Children's Army Universal Donation, Fudan Middle School had the best results with over 800 yuan. The other schools, including Minli Middle School, Southeast Women's Physical Education Teachers' School, Private Shanghai Middle School, Liangjiang Women's Physical Education Teachers' School, and Kaiming Middle School, also had over 600 yuan. Temporarily Suspends Business for Seven Days

Will Resume Business as Usual After Reorganization

Yong'an Silver Company, located at No. 473 North Sichuan Road in this city, was founded by Wang Jiazhen and others. It has not been established for even a few months. He Tianjian's Edited National Painting Monthly Second Issue Published

The National Painting Monthly published by the Chinese Calligraphy Association is edited by the famous painter He Tianjian and the famous art theory expert Xie Haiyan. The first issue has been sold out, and subscriptions continue to pour in. It has already been reprinted to avoid disappointing readers. The second issue is scheduled to be published on the 15th of this month. The content is even more exciting than the previous issue, with as many as eight illustrations of famous and valuable ancient paintings. Among them is Qiu Ying's Imitation of Longyan Fa's Qin Gathering Picture, which is specially printed as a large scroll 1 foot 2 inches long. This painting is Qiu Ying's masterpiece in his life and is rarely seen in the country. It can be hung for viewing or copied. The other paintings, such as those by Gao Fangshan, Zhou Dongcun, Dong Qichang, and Gong Banqian, are all authentic and exquisite. The texts include Chen Xiaodie's "Painting Theory from the Qing Dynasty," Huang Binhong's "Painting Method Infants Finger," Zheng Wuchang's "Responsibilities That Painters Should Bear," Wang Yachen's "On Wishes of Kai," Yu Jianhua's "Six Principles of Painting," He Tianjian's "Right and Wrong of Painting Societies and Styles," and "Painting History Rope," and other carefully crafted masterpieces. There are still more titles, which cannot be listed in detail. The annual subscription is 1.91 yuan, and individual copies are 1 dime each. For young people, this publication is no different from entering a correspondence school. Painters can get the opportunity to study. The general agent in Shanghai is Lu Chu's Shanghai Wang Pingheng Regular Script Printing Bureau. In North China, it is managed by the Dagongbao.

Famous Acupuncturist Lu Shouyan Excels at Treating Epilepsy and Mania

Mr. Lu Shouyan is the adopted son of Mr. Li Peiqing, a famous doctor in Jiading. He has been practicing medicine with his father in Shanghai for many years. He has a deep family background and rich experience. He is effective in treating all kinds of intractable diseases such as paralysis and numbness. He is especially skilled in treating epilepsy and mania. It is said that the son of Mr. Zhu Jingcheng of the Sacred Mother's Hospital in this city has been suffering from illness for many years. He has been treated by famous Chinese and Western doctors, but to no avail. Later, through the introduction of the national doctor Hong Songjiong, he sought treatment from Dr. Lu at Fude Lane in the West of the Eight Immortals Bridge in the French Concession. After the doctor used his wonderful acupuncture techniques, the patient's mind immediately cleared up, and after only a few treatments, the illness suddenly disappeared. The doctor's amazing skills are truly the savior of those suffering from mania.

Tongchang Thermos Factory, located in Lion Lane, Nine Acres, produces one-pound leather belt military thermos bottles, two-pound large Tzubei and Bakelite cup thermos bottles, and four-pound spray-painted thermos bottles. Upon hearing the news, people from all walks of life gathered to purchase them, and there is a general shortage of supply.

Summary of Bank Inspection Reports

Central Bank Issue Reserve 217th Inspection Report: According to Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this committee is responsible for inspecting the reserve funds for the exchange of banknotes issued by the bank. The 217th inspection was conducted on October 10th, 23rd year of the Republic of China at the bank's issuing bureau. The inspection results are announced as follows: (A) Total amount of exchange banknotes issued: 87,911,710 silver yuan, including 81,648,604 silver yuan banknotes and 6,263,106 subsidiary coin banknotes. Total amount of exchange banknote reserves: 87,911,710 yuan, including 69,933,710 yuan in cash reserves. This cash reserve includes 65,367,303 yuan stored in the bank's issuing vault, 2,697,593 yuan stored in branch banks in various ports, and 1,868,814 yuan stored with counterpart banks. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 17,978,000 silver yuan. (B) Total amount of customs gold exchange banknotes issued: 373,324.7 yuan of customs gold. Total amount of customs gold exchange banknote reserves: 373,324.7 yuan of customs gold. This reserve includes 7,351 taels, 9 mace, and 5 fen of standard gold, equivalent to 373,324.7 yuan of customs gold at the fixed price of 5 orders and 779. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank Exchange Banknote Regulations, 60% is cash reserve and 40% is guarantee reserve. The results of this inspection show that the cash exceeds 60% and the guarantee is less than 40%, which is in line with the regulations. This report is made. December 11, 23rd year of the Republic of China, Li Fusun, Chairman of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank, Xie Mingxun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jilong.

The Four Banks Reserve Treasury is jointly established by the Salt Industry, Jin Cheng, Zhongnan, and Continental Four Banks. It specializes in issuing banknotes for the Zhongnan Bank. According to the treasury's issuing regulations, banknotes are issued with full reserves. The cash reserve is at least 60%, and the guarantee reserve is at most 40%. An announcement is made every week, and it is audited by the auditors and accountants of the Four Banks. The 258th announcement of the Shanghai Reserve Treasury on December 8, 23rd year of the Republic of China, is recorded as follows: Amount of banknotes in circulation: 31,392,373 yuan. Total amount of reserves: 31,392,373 yuan, including cash reserves of 24,412,593 yuan and guarantee reserves of 7,266,450 yuan.

Six Lost Boys and Girls Waiting to be Claimed

Six lost boys and girls, including Li Ming (male, 13 years old, from Sichuan), Liu Xianting (male, 13 years old, from Hubei), Zhang Zongyou (male, 15 years old, from Changxing), Liu Jianglin (male, 17 years old, from Rugao), Yang Cuidi (female, 8 years old, from Jiangbei), and Yang Xiaoliuzi (male, 5 years old, from Jiangbei), were found crying and lost in the French Concession between the 5th and 9th of this month. The patrolmen found them one after another and brought them to the police station. Due to language barriers or the inability to provide their addresses, their families could not be found. The head of the police station ordered them to be temporarily kept, waiting for their families to claim them. If any families have lost children and see this report, they can go to the French General Police Station in Lujiazui to claim them.

Publishing World

▲ Lingkuixuan Literary Manuscripts Published: Mr. Ye Guisun of Tongcheng has been studying ancient prose for forty years. His writing style is elegant, and his emotions are deep and beautiful. His uncle, Ting Sheng, was a high-ranking official in the Ministry of Personnel and a prominent disciple of Yao Shifu. Mr. Ye has been familiar with the discussions of his local predecessors since childhood. He was first appreciated by Mr. Wu Zhipu, and later followed Mr. Ma Tongbo, making profound progress. Tong Lao said that his best works often resemble those of Ou Gui. After the age of fifty, his works became even more elegant and淡泊. Recently, he has been residing in Shanghai, enduring poverty and concealing his talents. Many people have been seeking to have his works published. His disciples have been troubled by the copying of his rough drafts. His son, Yinggen, has published dozens of his father's articles. They are now available for sale at Qingyi Bookstore on Simalu and Lili Literary Company on Qipan Street, Sijing Road. Each copy is only priced at four dimes.

▲ New Fortress Literary Monthly Creation Special Issue: The New Fortress Literary Monthly, which is known as a lone fighter in the Chinese literary world, has seen a sharp increase in sales since the last addition of the drawing section and the refreshing of the internal space. This shows that the magazine's efforts have been deeply appreciated by readers. The magazine recently moved to a new office at No. 221 Shandong Road due to the rapid development of its affairs. It has decided to publish a Creation Special Issue in the sixth issue of the fourth volume to show even greater efforts. It is said that the special issue was published yesterday. In addition to the unchanged original drawing section, Tan Cong, and Outpost sections, the rest includes Tie Mingde, Yidan Yi, Gu Hesheng's [Illness], Meng Bai's [Sister-in-law], Zheng Bo's [Pirate], Ding Di's [Wan Guiyou], Wu Yuan's [Secret of the Island], the 13th creation is priced as usual at two dimes per issue, one yuan and one dime for half a year, and two yuan for a full year. The Times Book Company is the general agent.

The first issue of the second volume has now been published. ▲ China Newspaper and Magazine Guide Published: Mr. Lin Zhangbin, the owner of the China Commercial Advertising Company at No. 40 Hong Kong Road in this city, realized that Chinese and foreign merchants need a thorough understanding of the publication situation of Chinese and Western newspapers and magazines in China and Hong Kong for reference in advertising planning. Therefore, based on his more than ten years of experience in advertising, he conducted a recent comprehensive survey and wrote the China Newspaper and Magazine Guide in English. The entire book, including the appendix index, has a total of 130 pages. The newspapers and magazines listed, both Chinese and Western, are included without omission. They are listed according to province and city. Detailed descriptions are included of the population, products, and transportation of the province, city, county, and town. A national general map and provincial maps of the publication's location are included. Detailed records are provided for the nature of the newspaper or magazine, its recent sales, and the size of each column and various special publications. An index is appended to the end of the book for the convenience of the reader. It is truly a necessary reference book for the industrial and commercial community and scholars of business administration. The book is printed on high-quality white Dowling paper and bound in Western style. It sells for five yuan per copy. Those who wish to purchase it can go directly to the bookstore of the company on Hong Kong Road to purchase it.

The director is Ying Yunwei, and the main actors are Yuan Muzhi and Chen Bo'er. Although they are newcomers to the film industry, they have long had a considerable position in the drama world. The success of this film is even more unexpected than we thought. It is rumored that it will be publicly screened at the theatre soon.

Medical World

▲ Achievements of Young Doctor Li Zhonglu: The young doctor Li Zhonglu is the son of the famous doctor Li Menghua of Baitang. He specializes in internal and surgical medicine. He participated in the revolution in his early years. After the Northern Expedition, he devoted himself to medicine and worked hard at the first and second National Medical and Pharmaceutical Group Representatives Conferences. Most of the local medical and pharmaceutical construction projects in this county were carried out by him. This summer, he was hired by the Shanghai Municipal Construction Factory Association to serve as a medical consultant, saving countless lives. Zhang Xinbao, a construction industry operator, happened to fall ill at the Ningbo branch factory and, admiring Dr. Li's reputation, specifically asked to return to Shanghai for treatment. After being treated, he recovered from his illness in less than ten days. The clinic is located at No. 12 Tianyou Lane, Xujiahui.

Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Six: The Poor Girl Dislikes The West Tutor

When she was feeling extremely upset, Zhu Yueying smoothed out her face with an even layer of powder. She dipped the powder puff into the powder jar and said to Xiao Ji, "I've done everything you told me to. What else is there to say?" Xiao Ji had originally wanted to say a few more words to her, but then he thought, it was already hard enough to get her to this point. If he said something that upset her, and she refused to go to the front, then all his efforts would be in vain. So, he smiled at her and said, "You're very clever. Just touch up your face a bit. That's enough. There's no need to overdo it. I'll take you there." Auntie Hu heard this and came over to pull Yueying's sleeve, smiling and whispering, "Go on, it's alright. I'll be with you." Yueying lowered her head and followed the direction of her pull, slowly walking while holding onto the wall. When Auntie Hu pulled her into the courtyard, she flung her hand away, pulled her sleeve back, and said with her head slightly lowered, "I'm not a little child of three or two years old. What do I need you to hold me for?" Auntie Hu looked back at her, and she saw that her cheeks were puffed up. Auntie Hu stopped and said to her, "That's not right of you. Not counting our family, you still have two family members closely following behind you, all hoping that you can find them a way to make a living. If you go to see people looking like you're collecting debts, how will they be happy? Even like this, can things be done? It's not that I, as your aunt, want to interfere in your affairs. Who told your three generations to come all the way here to find me? If you don't want to do this, I don't want to do this even more." As she spoke, she slowly lowered her expression, and continued, "You don't have to go then. Your three generations can take flight and go far away. Don't come and burden me, this pitiful person." (87) ▲Yesterday's number should be changed to [86]

A Group of Street Artists

— Xunzi

Walking along Avenue Joffre, to the west of the Empire Theater, there is a horizontal street where a very famous temple in Shanghai is located, called Guoren Temple. Opposite it is a French Catholic church. Facing each other, the religions are different, the nationalities are different, and the colors are not harmonious. The two buildings are forever facing each other in silence.

Because both sides are surrounded by walls, the cement sidewalk is occupied by street artists as their territory. A man in his fifties, with a mustache like the Chinese character "eight" on his lip, sat listlessly on a bench. On a board table in front of him were all his tools of the trade. It turned out he was a character splitter who also wrote letters for people. Although it was early, !twelve o'clock noon!, there was already a female patron engaging him to write a letter. The patron, with her plump figure and several pure gold rings on her fingers, quite large, showed her wealth. She looked like an old madam from a "wild chicken" brothel. Because she was from Yangzhou and the character splitter was from Shaoxing, their dialects were different, so every sentence they wrote required several back-and-forth entanglements.

On the cement, four words written in white powder, "Open-air Stage", circled a large pair of artists of the opposite sex. The man had a sparse fake beard hanging from his lips, and his nose was smeared with white powder and black ink, symbolizing a clown on the stage. He also had a small braid sticking up on his forehead. He was shaking a broken palm-leaf fan in his hand. One moment he made jokes and gestures, the next he hummed a "Xipi Yaoban" tune, busy enough to have beads of sweat oozing from his skin. The woman standing next to him was still dressed normally, without makeup, but her clothes were shiny and greasy, like a barber's cloth for shaving heads, and her face was the color of paper ingots. Although her hair had not been cut, it was as loose and messy as a pile of firewood, fully revealing that she was a believer in morphine and heroin. She was keeping time with the male performer's lyrics, playing a erhu. When it was her turn to open her mouth, she would also hum a few lines, surprisingly accurate and clear, without any dissonance. The audience standing there, because they were of the opposite sex, shouted "Bravo!" like crazy.

On this cement sidewalk, there were a total of three or four open-air stages like this, performed by men and women together. Because going to the theater to listen to a play cost at least ten cents, but here, you only needed one copper coin to listen to your fill, so their livelihood was not bad.

There were also several storytellers who had not apprenticed to a master, nor had they joined any Guangyu or Runyu societies. Just because they were poor and down on their luck, they relied on old novels like "The Biography of Ji Gong" and "Lu Sheng Dan," which they had read fluently, and shamelessly told stories on this cement sidewalk. They also wrote on the ground, "So-and-so is telling "The Biography of Ji Gong," etc." Each listener was charged one copper coin, which was not too expensive, and it was a unique way to make a living.

This street was very lively because it was where these artists were active. If you haven't had the chance to see it, you might as well go and observe it. Those who study sociology can get a lot of information there.

Tidbits

— (Yan Xinquan)

Two farmers are preparing to plow their fields, hoping for heavy rains in the coming days. One is preparing to dry rice to make rice, hoping for several days of good sunshine. The weather under these circumstances, of course, makes one farmer happy and the other resentful. It is the same in life sometimes.

The Faint Fragrance of Royal Incense

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

After we heard this, although we all knew that the Empress Dowager was speaking, especially the last sentence, which was absolutely contrary to the facts: but who would dare to openly refute her? The Empress Dowager herself had long expected that no one would dare to be so bold. However, her favorite servant, Li Lianying, had already made a look between his eyebrows, ready to speak for the Empress Dowager at any time. He had seen very little of the Xianfeng Emperor's affairs with his own eyes, and he knew that Xianfeng was not a wise monarch; however, in order to ingratiate himself with the Empress Dowager, he deliberately pretended to be always on the Empress Dowager's side, and if any of us dared to challenge her, he would definitely deny the facts and support the Empress Dowager to the end. But fortunately! None of us were brave enough, and no one dared to say a word in the end, so Li Lianying's loyal heart had no way to express itself, which was very disappointing for him.

After the Empress Dowager made this forced explanation, the melancholy and depression in her heart seemed to have dissipated by half. Unexpectedly, such self-deceptive words can sometimes give oneself some comfort. She turned back again and looked at the few relics, as if she felt satisfied: then she slowly raised her head, with a kind of pitiable arrogance, and gave me a faint smile. Her meaning seemed to be:

[Don't look at his relics being so few, he was still an emperor in his lifetime!] In this way, we left this main hall, turned a corner, and walked into a main hall in the same palace courtyard; the Empress Dowager was still leading the way in front, but we all knew where she was going now, so we were even more cautious and absolutely didn't say a word. It turned out that we were now going to the place where the Tongzhi Emperor's relics were stored! (197)

The Wild Monk

— Shen Yu

On the west side of Rotten Flagpole Bridge stands a dilapidated temple that has been forgotten by people. The temple's incense has long been extinguished; the [resident monk] also disappeared many years ago. Therefore, it has become a place for wandering monks to rest temporarily.

Since autumn began, more than ten monks have been staying overnight in that dilapidated temple. Their daily lives are a dual personality. If you don't believe it, listen to me tell you:

These many monks, during the day, disperse into various villages. Each of their costumes has a commonality: on their backs they all have a [Weituo] pasted, this [Weituo] is installed in a wooden frame; on the frame are also inserted three sticks of incense; on their chests they all hang a large wooden fish. When they arrive in front of each family's door, they immediately kneel on the ground, then raise the wooden mallet, knock out [peeling peeling] sounds, while muttering sutras in their mouths; and also kowtow three times. Then they move to another house, performing the same [pathetic show].

After three or four days, they take advantage of their [lack of fate] to go to the homes they had chanted in front of, claiming to be from [Hangzhou] or [Putuo]; and saying that a certain temple there had [collapsed walls], or that a bridge there had [been in disrepair for years], so they came specifically to solicit donations to rebuild the temple and repair the bridge.

Honestly speaking, the people in the countryside all believe in [gods and Buddhas], so they believe without doubt, and donate according to their ability.

After they collect the money, they buy some white wine and fresh meat in the nearby town. Then, the dilapidated temple suddenly becomes lively, everyone eating and drinking, enjoying themselves like they are bewitched. Really, sometimes they even play gambling games!

All Rights Reserved

— Yue

▲Thank you for the gift of Qing Dynasty Diplomatic Historical Materials: Qing Dynasty's important diplomatic documents, should not be publicized as a rule. In the past, diplomatic works were often based on foreign sources, resulting in obscuration and incomprehension of the truth, which readers criticized. Recently, Mr. Wang Xiyin of the Diplomatic Historical Materials Compilation Office, No. 7 Guandongdian, Beiping, with the efforts of two generations of father and son, has compiled Diplomatic Historical Materials of the Guangxu and Xuantong Dynasties of the Qing Dynasty, which has been completed. The manuscript is based on current secret documents from the Qing Military Aircraft Department and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, as well as archives from overseas embassies, which are detailed, accurate, and worthy of study. The office has also recently compiled four volumes of the Qing Dynasty Diplomatic Yearbook, which have been published together. The entire book consists of more than 160 volumes, and the special price is 90 yuan. Our library's reference department was given a volume, so we hereby acknowledge with thanks.

Small Recipe

Miscellaneous Notes on Tonics

— Zhu Yun

In this year of drought, the countryside is declaring bankruptcy, and in the cities, all industries are declining, presenting a desolate scene. Lively streets often have vacant shops. In this recession, even white rice is becoming a problem. What spare money is there to study tonics? However, strolling through the streets and alleys, wooden boxes of XX Ranch Consumptive Milk can be seen everywhere, and soy milk and cod liver oil are also experiencing a surge in sales. [Poor, poor, poor, still have three loads of copper]; moreover, our country is vast and rich in resources; [only with a healthy body can one do healthy things], the season is turning to winter, and there are many weak people who need to take some tonics to restore their health!

Zhu is just a poor scholar who, in this environment of rice as precious as pearls and firewood as expensive as cinnamon, relies on a worn-out pen to maintain the life of a poor couple, and is indeed stretched thin and in dire straits! However, due to several illnesses and once coughing up blood, his weak body, due to the persuasion of relatives and friends and his wife's frugality, has also been taking tonics in this early winter season. This is truly a laughable and lamentable farce! But thanks to the benefits of this weak body, he has come to know a few tonics, and dares not keep them secret, writing them out for fellow sufferers to adopt.

The most economical and effective tonic is, of course, soy milk mixed with raw eggs. Soy milk is readily available for sale in tofu shops, three copper coins for a full bowl. Eggs cost sixty coppers per yuan, and eating four a day is only ten coppers. The monthly cost, combined, is only one dollar and thirty cents, but its tonic power is very effective. This is truly a tonic for the common people. A slightly more expensive tonic than soy milk and eggs is cod liver oil. The tonic power of pure cod liver oil is very great, and its value is also very low. Five pounds can be had for one dollar and fifty cents, with each pound costing only about thirty cents, which cannot be considered anything but an inexpensive tonic. However, the smell of pure cod liver oil is unusually fishy and foul, and people with poor appetites find it difficult to drink. Therefore, other tonics are added to the fish oil to eliminate the fishy smell: milk is added to fish liver oil, making it white, called [milky white cod liver oil]; malt extract is added, making it brown, called [malt extract cod liver oil]. These types of cod liver oil are readily available for sale in pharmacies, but they cost four or five times more than pure cod liver oil.

Milk is also a common tonic. The milk carried and delivered by farmers is very cheap, with half a pound in a bottle costing only about one dollar and forty cents per month. However, this type of milk is delivered directly by farmers, and whether it is mixed with soy milk and whether the disinfection is complete, makes those who value hygiene afraid to take it greedily and fearlessly.

In addition to milk, there are also two types of beef juice and chicken juice. These two types of tonics, because chicken juice costs twelve dollars a month, and beef juice is avoided by some weak people in Suzhou who abstain from eating it, have not seen strong sales. Recently in Suzhou, chickens cost four catties for one yuan, and a single chicken costs only about one thousand cash. Buying the chicken yourself and boiling it into chicken juice is half the price of buying it ready-made, and the juice is thicker and there is more water, and the chicken meat can still be used as a snack, which is much more economical.

Our country's tonics are truly numerous and expensive. Those ginseng, bird's nests, deer antlers, and turtle shells are not only expensive, but also difficult to take. The ordinary ones are still silver ears. Ordinary silver ears cost about four yuan per tael. Slightly swell the dried silver ears in water, add rock sugar, and simmer in water over low heat. The procedure is not very tedious, but the taste is very sweet and delicious. The taste of hasma is similar to that of silver ears, but when eating it, first soak the muscles of the hasma until they swell, and the blood vessels attached to the meat must be removed one by one with silver needles before cooking. Yellow lip maw is also a tonic comparable to ginseng; to eat it, first use a ring to make the huge fish maw into thin strips, soak them until they swell, and then simmer them with rice to make porridge, which has a slightly fishy taste. In addition, there are also shark fins, mutton cakes, etc. The methods of eating are mostly like cooking dishes, either boiled in plain water or braised in soy sauce, each according to their preference. When a person really reaches the point where medicine is ineffective, if tonics can really bring the dead back to life, then the lives of the poor will be even more worthless. As the saying goes: [Rice is nourishing and meat builds muscle], those hard-working laborers, their spirits are much stronger than those who take tonics every day!
